## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt with features (t, P) is a continuous-time population dynamics task: the growth rate depends on current population size (density dependence) and possibly explicit time forcing (seasonality or changing environment). Common models express dP_dt as birth–death balance with linear, nonlinear, saturating, or threshold (Allee) dependence on P, sometimes with time-varying parameters via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear birth–death with constant immigration/harvest: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net proportional growth plus constant source/sink)
- Density-dependent (quadratic) logistic rate form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying capacity via negative quadratic term)
- General polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (empirical birth–death closure; can encode Allee/overcompensation)
- Gompertz growth (log-density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(c2 * P)) (decelerating growth with log feedback; c2 scales P to be dimensionless)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible curvature of approach to carrying capacity)
- Saturating per-capita growth (Monod-like in P): dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (crowding reduces growth rate via saturation)
- Ricker-type continuous form (overcompensation): dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (strong density dependence producing peaked net growth)
- Allee effect (strong Allee with carrying capacity): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative at low P and high P, positive in-between)
- Pure harvesting/effort mortality (proportional): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P (net growth reduced by constant per-capita removal)
- Harvesting with saturation (effort-limited removal): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P / (1 + c2 * P) (removal increases then saturates with P)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (time-periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (time-varying intrinsic growth with carrying capacity feedback)
- Trend in environment (nonstationary r): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P * (1 - c2 * P) (slow directional change in growth conditions)
- Time-dependent carrying capacity (K(t) encoded via coefficient): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * P) (seasonally varying crowding constraint)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Carrying capacity behavior (growth turns negative at high P) typically appears as a negative higher-order term in P, e.g., dP_dt includes -c * P**2 or a factor (1 - c * P).
- Allee effects (negative growth at low P) often require at least a quadratic factor in P beyond the trivial P factor, creating an interior unstable equilibrium, e.g., P * (c * P - 1).
- Gompertz-like deceleration is indicated by log terms (per-capita growth decreases roughly linearly with log(P)), suggesting dP_dt proportional to P * (const - log(c * P)).
- Overcompensatory density dependence (peaked growth then sharp decline) is often represented by P * exp(-c * P) rather than a simple quadratic, producing a unimodal dP_dt vs P.
- Explicit seasonality or periodic forcing in time is suggested by sinusoidal dependence in coefficients multiplying P and/or (1 - c * P), e.g., (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * ...
- Nonstationary environments (long-term change) are captured by slow trends in time within parameters, such as (c0 + c1 * t) multiplying the P-dependent structure.
- If data show near-zero growth around a typical P level with symmetric deviations, a polynomial in P around that scale (linear + quadratic + cubic) can approximate net birth–death balance locally.
- A constant offset term (+c1) in dP_dt can represent immigration/stocking or constant harvesting; its necessity is indicated if dP_dt is nonzero near P ≈ 0.
- Saturating removal or saturation of per-capita growth with P is naturally encoded via rational forms like P/(1 + c * P), which prevent unbounded per-capita rates at high P.

============================================================

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG5)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4/(c5*P + c6)
Candidate formulas: 95

GT (fixed):
\[
0.9198344660\,(1-\tfrac{P}{84.0283518631})P \;+\; 0.9198344660\,\frac{P^2}{7.5314755755\,P+1}
\]
Rewrite structure:
- Polynomial part: \(0.9198344660\,P - \frac{0.9198344660}{84.0283518631}P^2\). So it is **linear + quadratic** with fixed coefficients.
- Rational part: \(0.9198344660\,\dfrac{P^2}{7.5314755755 P+1}\). This is of the form \(\dfrac{A P^2}{B P + 1}\) (no constant numerator term, no \(P^3\) term).

So overall GT is:
\[
(\alpha P^2 + \beta P) \;+\; \frac{\gamma P^2}{\delta P + 1}
\]
with \(\alpha\neq 0,\beta\neq 0,\gamma\neq 0,\delta\neq 0\), and **no** extra constants, sines, logs, exponentials, \(1/P\), etc.

Now check candidates for whether they can be parameter-set to exactly this form (possibly after combining like terms), allowing domain restrictions if needed.

---

### 1
Has extra \(P*c4 + P*c5\) (can be merged into linear term), plus sinusoid \(c6\sin(\cdot)\) and constant \(c9\). Set \(c6=0,c9=0\). Then it becomes
\(P^2 c0 + P(c1+c4+c5) + \frac{P c2}{P c3+1}\).
But GT needs \(\frac{P^2}{\delta P+1}\), not \(\frac{P}{\delta P+1}\). Cannot fix by constants. **No**.

### 2
Similarly has \(\frac{c3}{P c4+1}\) (no \(P^2\) numerator) and optional sine. Even with sine off, rational term is wrong power. **No**.

### 3
Contains \(t\) in exponent via sine; to remove, set \(c4=0\) (or exponent 0), leaving polynomial only, but GT has rational term. **No**.

### 4
All terms share denominator \((P c1+1)\) and include \(P^3\) numerator term. GT is “polynomial + rational”, not a single rational with possible \(P^3\) unless it cancels. You could set \(c0=0\) to remove \(P^3\), but then everything is \(\frac{\text{poly in }P}{P c1+1}\) with no separate polynomial part. That cannot equal GT’s polynomial-plus-rational decomposition for all \(P\) on any interval (it would imply GT is a single rational function). GT is not a single rational because it has an explicit polynomial part plus a rational part with same denominator? Actually GT’s rational denominator is \((7.531...P+1)\); if you put GT over that denominator you get a cubic numerator, so GT *is* a single rational. But candidate 4’s numerator degrees/coeff freedom: it yields \(\frac{aP^3+bP^2+cP}{dP+1}\) (no constant term). GT when combined:
\[
(\alpha P^2+\beta P) + \frac{\gamma P^2}{\delta P+1}
= \frac{(\alpha P^2+\beta P)(\delta P+1)+\gamma P^2}{\delta P+1}
= \frac{\alpha\delta P^3 + (\alpha+\beta\delta+\gamma)P^2 + \beta P}{\delta P+1}
\]
This has **no constant term** indeed. So candidate 4 potentially can match by choosing:
- denominator slope \(c1=\delta\)
- \(c0=\alpha\delta\)
- sum of its \(P^2\) coefficients equals \(\alpha+\beta\delta+\gamma\)
- sum of its \(P\) coefficients equals \(\beta\)
Candidate 4 has enough free parameters to set those sums. Therefore **YES, candidate 4 can match**.

(We don’t even need domain restrictions; it can match as rational identity where denominator nonzero.)

### 5
Also single rational over \((P c1+1)\) with a \(P^3\) term coefficient \(c0\) and many adjustable \(P^2,P\) terms plus an extra fixed \(+ P/(P c1+1)\) (but that’s just another \(P\) coefficient effectively). Still can fit the same target \(\frac{aP^3+bP^2+cP}{dP+1}\). So **YES**.

### 6
Form: \(P^2 c0 + P(c1+c2) + \frac{P c3}{P c4+1}\). Rational numerator is \(P\), not \(P^2\). **No**.

### 7
Like 4 but missing one \(P\) term; still has enough \(P\)-coefficient freedom (multiple \(P\) terms) and \(P^2\) terms. It yields \(\frac{aP^3+bP^2+cP}{dP+1}\). **YES**.

### 8
Polynomial + \(\frac{P c2}{P c3+1}\) again wrong numerator power. **No**.

### 9
Has \(\frac{P c2}{P c3+c4} + \frac{c6}{P c3+c4}\) giving \(\frac{(c2 P + c6)}{c3 P + c4}\), not \(\frac{P^2}{\delta P+1}\). Can’t make numerator \(P^2\). **No**.

### 10
Single rational over \((P c1+1)\) including possible constant-over-denominator terms \(c8/(...)+c9/(...)\) which can be set to 0. Then same as candidate 4 class. **YES**.

### 11
Has \(\frac{P c4}{P c5+1}\) (numerator \(P\)), not \(P^2\). **No**.

### 12
Same family as 10 (single rational with adjustable coefficients). Set \(c9=0\) if needed. **YES**.

### 13
Same family as 5 with extra constant-over-denominator \(c7/(...)\) set to 0. **YES**.

### 14
Has \(\frac{P c2}{P c3+1}\) wrong power. **No**.

### 15
Has \(P*c1/(P*c2+1)\) (numerator \(P\)), not \(P^2\). **No**.

### 16
Has \(\frac{P c2}{P c3+1}\) wrong power. **No**.

### 17
Has \(\frac{P c4}{P c5+1}\) wrong power. **No**.

### 18
Has \(\frac{P c2}{P c3+1}\) wrong power. **No**.

### 19
Same issue. **No**.

### 20
Has \(\frac{c4}{P c5+1}\) (constant numerator), not \(P^2\). **No**.

### 21
Has \(\frac{P c3}{P c4+1}\) wrong power. **No**.

### 22
Has \(\frac{P c4}{P c5+c6} + \frac{c7}{P c5+c6}\) giving numerator linear in \(P\), not quadratic. **No**.

### 23
Has \(\frac{P c2}{P c3+1}\) wrong power; extra \(P^{c6}\) term can be killed. Still wrong. **No**.

### 24
Has \(\frac{P c3}{P c4+1}\) wrong power. **No**.

### 25
Same wrong power. **No**.

### 26
Has \(\frac{c3}{P c4+1}\) wrong power. **No**.

### 27–35
Contain logs/exp or additional rational pieces not matching; even if those are zeroed, the remaining rational term is typically \(\frac{P c}{P c+1}\) or \(\frac{c}{P c+1}\), not \(\frac{P^2}{\delta P+1}\). **No** for 27–35.

### 36
Has extra \(\frac{P c6}{P c7+1}\) but still only \(P\) numerators. Could we combine two \(P/(aP+1)\) terms to get \(P^2/(aP+1)\)? No: sum of such terms stays of form \(\frac{P(\cdots)}{(aP+1)(bP+1)}\) unless same denominator; if same denominator, it’s still \(\frac{P\cdot K}{aP+1}\), not \(P^2\). **No**.

### 37–45
Same mismatch (wrong rational numerator power, or extra non-algebraic terms). **No**.

### 46–50
Include logs or \(1/P\) terms; cannot match GT (GT has no \(1/P\), no logs). **No**.

### 51
No rational term. **No**.

### 52–95
All include \(t\)-dependent terms, logs/exp/sin, or inverse powers; you could set their coefficients to 0 to remove \(t\), but then you’re left with either pure polynomial or the wrong rational structure (typically \(P/(aP+1)\) or constants). None introduce exactly \(\frac{P^2}{aP+1}\) in addition to a polynomial except the “all-over-one-denominator” family already identified (4,5,7,10,12,13). So **No** for 52–95.

## Explicit matching construction (for the matching candidates)
Let GT combined into one rational:
\[
\frac{A P^3 + B P^2 + C P}{\delta P + 1}
\]
where
- \(\delta = 7.531475575495239\)
- \(\alpha = -0.9198344660444582/84.0283518630852\)
- \(\beta = 0.9198344660444582\)
- \(\gamma = 0.9198344660444582\)
and
- \(A=\alpha\delta\)
- \(B=\alpha+\beta\delta+\gamma\)
- \(C=\beta\)

Candidates 4/5/7/10/12/13 can represent \(\frac{aP^3+bP^2+cP}{dP+1}\) by setting their shared denominator parameter \(c1=d=\delta\), choosing \(c0=a=A\), and setting the sums of their \(P^2\) coefficients to \(b=B\) and sums of their \(P\) coefficients to \(c=C\), with any extra constant-over-denominator terms set to 0 where present.

Thus at least one candidate (indeed several) can be made exactly equal to GT (on domain \(P\neq -1/\delta\), which is a standard plausible continuous domain restriction).
